### Round 1 | planner | planner_initial

- diagnosis: Task: infer the most likely AIE mechanism class (ICT vs TICT vs ESIPT vs neutral aromatic) for the provided C82H58N4S polyaromatic with many phenyl rings and multiple tertiary anilines plus an N–S–N heteroring. Top1 working hypothesis is TICT because the prepared-structure context indicates many rotatable bonds (16) and a large multi-aryl donor-rich scaffold where twisted conformations can open non-radiative decay channels in dilute solution; aggregation would restrict these motions and suppress TICT-like quenching. Runner-up is neutral aromatic/RIM without dominant CT, since the system is also highly aromatic and may emit from locally excited states with aggregation-enhanced rigidity/packing. Top1 is uncertain because we have not yet established whether S1 has substantial charge-transfer character and whether the emitting state is twisted vs more locally excited; both TICT and neutral-aromatic RIM can look similar at a high level for large multi-phenyl luminogens. Evidence that would separate them: (i) computed S1 electron–hole separation / oscillator strength trends consistent with CT, (ii) S1 geometry showing increased twisting at donor–acceptor junctions, (iii) qualitative orbital localization (HOMO on donors, LUMO on acceptor/heteroring) vs more delocalized LE. Shared prepared structure is available (SDF/XYZ; conformer_id=4). Macro can do fast structure-feature reasoning and propose discriminating signatures; Microscopic can run exactly one bounded baseline S0 optimization plus S1 vertical excitation on the shared structure to extract CT indicators (e.g., excitation character, oscillator strength, frontier orbitals). First round should gather both: macro priors are strong for rotor-driven AIE, while a single baseline quantum snapshot can quickly indicate whether ICT/TICT is genuinely prominent versus mostly neutral aromatic LE/RIM.

- action: macro_and_microscopic

- confidence: 0.52

- task_instruction: Run first-round macro + one bounded microscopic baseline to characterize whether S1 is CT-like (supporting ICT/TICT) or more locally excited (supporting neutral aromatic/RIM).

- reasoning_summary: From the shared structure context, the molecule is a very large, highly aromatic, heavily substituted multi-aryl system (145 atoms; 14 aromatic rings; 13 ring systems) with multiple aryl–aryl linkages and a moderate number of rotatable bonds (16). This “rotor-rich” topology is consistent with the *possibility* of twisted conformations and intramolecular rotation (a prerequisite for TICT-like behavior), but the reported high planarity/compactness proxies (planarity_proxy ~0.974; compactness_proxy ~0.959) suggest the selected conformer is globally fairly planar/compact rather than strongly orthogonalized donor–acceptor subunits. Hetero atom count is low (5) and the donor/acceptor partition proxy is only moderate (~0.5), implying limited polarity contrast for a strong, classical donor–acceptor charge-transfer axis. Net: the structure supports “many torsions available” (compatible with twisting), but does not, on these proxies alone, strongly evidence a dedicated D–A TICT motif; it remains equally plausible that AIE arises from generic restriction of intramolecular motion in a large multi-phenyl framework.
Capability limit note: This macro pass can only reuse provided structure prep outputs and deterministic topology/geometry proxies; it cannot compute excited-state charge transfer, dihedral potential surfaces, solvent effects, or aggregation/packing energetics needed to confirm TICT.

- diagnosis: Round 4/20 (17 remaining). Top1=neutral aromatic (0.52) vs Top2=TICT (0.25). Latest evidence (torsion-dependent S1–S5 vertical manifolds on one high-relevance aryl–aryl dihedral) strengthens neutral aromatic relative to TICT: as the dihedral is twisted, S1 oscillator strength decreases dramatically (f: ~0.684 at 0°, 0.607 at 30°, 0.366 at 60°, ~0.0001 at 90°, then partially recovers ~0.387 at 120°), consistent with conjugation disruption/darkening, while no clear hallmark of TICT state reordering to a new low-lying CT/dark state is demonstrated by the provided summary. TICT is weakened but not eliminated because only one junction was probed and TICT could occur at a different donor–acceptor-like torsion. ICT remains a plausible third candidate but is limited by missing CT descriptors. Key remaining discriminator (neutral aromatic vs TICT): whether any other key dihedral(s) produce a low-lying dark state that becomes the new lowest state and correlates with a CT-like signature (e.g., dipole change/charge separation) rather than simple LE darkening from broken conjugation. Verifier supplementation remains missing (external retrieval still failing). Closure justification is collecting and improved internally (we now have one discriminative torsion manifold), but not yet sufficient for a decisive close because it sampled only one dihedral and did not include explicit CT metrics.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.52

### Round 5 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round budget: 5/20 (16 remaining). Top1=neutral aromatic (0.60) vs Top2=TICT (0.19). Latest evidence strengthens neutral aromatic: a second, distinct high-relevance aryl–aryl dihedral torsion scan (dih_29_30_31_32; 0–120°; S1–S5) again shows strong brightness modulation with near-zero f at ~90° while maintaining the qualitative pattern that the lowest state is the bright one at non-orthogonal angles (no clear CT/TICT-like state reordering demonstrated). This weakens TICT as the runner-up because the repeated observation across two different junctions is consistent with LE/conjugation-control darkening rather than a stabilized twisted-CT minimum becoming dominant. An additional candidate affected: ICT is slightly downweighted because CT-specific descriptors remain missing and the observed behavior can be explained without invoking CT stabilization. Key remaining discriminator between neutral aromatic and TICT: whether any other junction/conformer (especially closer to the NSNC-containing motif) produces a low-lying dark/CT state that becomes the lowest excited state upon twisting (state reordering) rather than merely reducing oscillator strength via conjugation break. Verifier supplementation remains missing (prior retrieval failures); closure justification is collecting but now materially improved (two dihedrals sampled) yet still not decisive for all torsional degrees of freedom. Next action chosen (microscopic) because one more targeted torsion snapshot on the most CT-likely remaining junction is the highest-leverage internal discriminator and does not depend on the stalled verifier pathway.

### Round 7 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 7/20 (14 remaining). Top1=neutral aromatic (0.74) vs Top2=ICT (0.09); TICT drops to 0.08. Latest evidence strengthens neutral aromatic: the 8-conformer S1–S5 bundle shows lowest_state_is_bright and small excitation spread (0.0317 eV), providing negative evidence for a conformer-enabled dark/CT-like S1. This weakens the prior runner-up (TICT) by closing the main escape hatch (alternate conformer hosting dark S1). ICT is slightly relatively favored vs TICT as a secondary possibility, since any remaining CT character (if present) could be more non-twisted/ICT-like, but direct CT descriptors remain unavailable. Key remaining discriminator (neutral aromatic vs ICT): presence of significant charge-transfer character in the bright S1 (e.g., solvatochromism/large dipole change or computed CT metrics). Verifier supplementation remains missing (backend failure), and closure justification is collecting but now much closer to sufficient for neutral aromatic vs TICT; remaining gap is mostly LE vs ICT nuance and environment sensitivity. Next best action is to attempt external verifier again only if backend/model-id is fixed; otherwise proceed with best-available internal closure narrative without further low-yield compute.

- confidence: 0.74

Provide a decision-oriented summary of which mechanism is more typical for this scaffold class and why, and any red-flag challenge signals against neutral aromatic.

### Round 10 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 10/20 (11 remaining). Top1=neutral aromatic (0.81) vs Top2=unknown (0.10); ICT is third (0.07). Latest evidence (new 5-state baseline bundle) reinforces that S1 is very bright (f~1.16) and remains the lowest bright state, aligning with an LE/neutral-aromatic picture and offering no support for TICT-like dark-state takeover. The main remaining discriminator is not TICT vs LE anymore (largely closed internally), but LE (neutral aromatic) vs a more CT-like bright ICT and/or environment-driven mechanisms (captured by unknown). Verifier supplementation remains missing due to repeated external retrieval failure (invalid model identifier). Closure justification for LE vs ICT remains blocked because CT-sensitive descriptors (NTO/CT fraction/hole–electron overlap) and solvent response are unavailable in current artifacts; internal evidence nevertheless strongly disfavors TICT and supports a robust bright LE-like lowest state. Best next action is to avoid repeating stalled verifier/CT-parsing routes and instead perform an internal closure-justification step that targets the current Top1 vs Top2 split (neutral aromatic vs unknown) by explicitly mapping what environment/aggregation signatures would be required to override the strong LE-like gas-phase evidence; this is best done via a bounded Macro synthesis of environment-sensitivity risk factors and testable predictions, since further microscopic compute without solvent/CT metrics has diminishing returns.

Do not recommend system-level next actions.

- reasoning_summary: From shared structure context, the molecule is a very large multi-aryl system (145 atoms; 14 aromatic rings; 16 rotatable bonds) with low hetero count (5) and moderate donor/acceptor partition proxy (~0.5). Geometry proxies indicate high planarity and compactness (planarity_proxy ~0.97, compactness ~0.96), suggesting a relatively rigid, extended π-system with limited strong polar functionality. This topology generally favors LE-like excitations and RIM-based AIE while making strong solvent-polarity-driven ICT/TICT less structurally compelling; however, the large π-surface and many aryl rings elevate the risk of aggregation-specific phenomena (excimer/exciplex emission, H/J aggregate shifts, strong concentration-dependent spectral changes) that can mimic or override simple RIM interpretations. Thus, the most diagnostic falsifiers are signatures of strong polarity-dependent CT (Lippert–Mataga, large Stokes shift changes, dual emission) and classic aggregate emission hallmarks (new broad red-shifted band at high concentration/solid, long lifetimes/structureless spectra, hysteresis), plus unusually strong viscosity dependence beyond what is expected from suppressing phenyl rotations.

Do not recommend system-level next actions.
Shared 3D structure context is available and reused from /datasets/workspace/mas_aie/var/runtime/tools/shared_structure/ef047ab58b56/prepared_structure.xyz.
This agent should only summarize low-cost structural evidence and should not make a global mechanism judgment or recommend a system-level next action.
Reasoning summary: From shared structure context, the molecule is a very large multi-aryl system (145 atoms; 14 aromatic rings; 16 rotatable bonds) with low hetero count (5) and moderate donor/acceptor partition proxy (~0.5). Geometry proxies indicate high planarity and compactness (planarity_proxy ~0.97, compactness ~0.96), suggesting a relatively rigid, extended π-system with limited strong polar functionality. This topology generally favors LE-like excitations and RIM-based AIE while making strong solvent-polarity-driven ICT/TICT less structurally compelling; however, the large π-surface and many aryl rings elevate the risk of aggregation-specific phenomena (excimer/exciplex emission, H/J aggregate shifts, strong concentration-dependent spectral changes) that can mimic or override simple RIM interpretations. Thus, the most diagnostic falsifiers are signatures of strong polarity-dependent CT (Lippert–Mataga, large Stokes shift changes, dual emission) and classic aggregate emission hallmarks (new broad red-shifted band at high concentration/solid, long lifetimes/structureless spectra, hysteresis), plus unusually strong viscosity dependence beyond what is expected from suppressing phenyl rotations.
Capability limit note: This macro step can only leverage shared prepared structure descriptors and deterministic topology/geometry-proxy reasoning. It cannot compute solvatochromic slopes, excited-state dipoles, CT fractions, exciton coupling, or model aggregate packing; therefore outputs are limited to structurally informed risk assessment and experimental falsification signatures.
